  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_829067d6-53c4-4c6f-8fd4-7e6846b07a60'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText4145006923078738563" style="display:none">The thrilling sequel to Jennifer A. Nielsen's blockbuster NEW YORK TIMES bestseller THE FALSE PRINCE -- now in paperback!<br /><br />A kingdom teetering on the brink of destruction. A king gone missing. Who will survive?<br /> Just weeks after Jaron has taken the throne, an assassination attempt forces him into a deadly situation. Rumors of a coming war are winding their way between the castle walls, and Jaron feels the pressure quietly mounting within Carthya. Soon, it becomes clear that deserting the kingdom may be his only hope of saving it. But the further Jaron is forced to run from his identity, the more he wonders if it is possible to go too far. Will he ever be able to return home again? Or will he have to sacrifice his own life in order to save his kingdom?<br /> The stunning second installment of The Ascendance Trilogy takes readers on a roller coaster ride of treason and murder, thrills and peril, as they journey with the Runaway King.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9652740542297873717">Just... Imogen and Jaron.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742621.gif' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742622.gif' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>..Why this star-crossed lovers situation?! Why Jennifer Nielsen?!?!?!?!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742623.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As if I haven't suffered enough from Percy and Annabeth at the end of The Mark of Athena. Sheesh. <br/><br/>Princess Amarinda is a nice young lady and all, I mean we simply cannot hate her. But come on... we all know Jaron and Imogen are MEANT to be together.<br/><br/>They are the couple right next to Percy and Annabeth.   <span id="freeText9652740542297873717" style="display:none">Just... Imogen and Jaron.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742621.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742622.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>..Why this star-crossed lovers situation?! Why Jennifer Nielsen?!?!?!?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384165ra/742623.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As if I haven't suffered enough from Percy and Annabeth at the end of The Mark of Athena. Sheesh. <br><br>Princess Amarinda is a nice young lady and all, I mean we simply cannot hate her. But come on... we all know Jaron and Imogen are MEANT to be together.<br><br>They are the couple right next to Percy and Annabeth. That's right, PERCABETH. <br><br>Now, I think Jennifer Nielsen did a wonderful job at recapturing Jaron's stubborn ignorance and short-tempered annoyance, yet his sensitive side and good heart holds true. The jokes are brilliant as usual from Jaron, it never fails to make me crack a smile. <br><br>And Roden... yes, we all agree that he was quite the annoying character, always in denial about the identity of Sage and Jaron. But as the story progresses, he will turn into a character presumed as a bad-ass in my dictionary.<br><br>I also adore Fink. In the beginning, you will immediately think this kid as the most annoying face of the planet. But he grows to be a boy that helps enlightens the dark and difficult times in Jaron's adventure with the pirates.<br><br>But I must say the tension was a lot more alive in The False Prince. The twist and turns were a lot more predictable in The Runaway King, but it is definitely a fun read. <br><br>This is the series I'm following while I wait in agonizing pain for my Heroes of Olympus to release every October of the year. <br>But now Imogen and Jaron have the cliche we-can't-be-together-because-our-worlds-are-different issue, I'm even more depressed. <br><br>Final book of The Ascendance Trilogy, I await you!<br></span>

<div id="review_591961482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/591961482" />
    <a title="jv poore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore"><img alt="jv poore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570108420p2/5157918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/591961482?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jv poore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jv poore" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore">jv poore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer591961482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6542010742364997916">Yesterday at the baseball game I was looking for a young friend, but her mom told me that she was in the car, reading. When she joined us, I asked what she was reading and her little face lit up when she said The Runaway King. Then she told me she already couldn't wait for the final book in this series. Since it so happens that I absolutely adore this trilogy, I sent it to her this morning. Along with one other treasure by Ms. Nielsen. And I am at least as excited as she will be.<br/>*************** </span>
  <span id="freeText6542010742364997916" style="display:none">Yesterday at the baseball game I was looking for a young friend, but her mom told me that she was in the car, reading. When she joined us, I asked what she was reading and her little face lit up when she said The Runaway King. Then she told me she already couldn't wait for the final book in this series. Since it so happens that I absolutely adore this trilogy, I sent it to her this morning. Along with one other treasure by Ms. Nielsen. And I am at least as excited as she will be.<br />*************** ******************** *******<br />Before the ink was dry on my glowing review of The False Prince, (the first in the Ascendance Trilogy), I was deep into The Runaway King. This is the second book in the Ascendance Trilogy and it is absolutely everything that I hope for in a continuation.<br /><br />We met King Jaron earlier, when he was Sage (aka Prince Jaron) hiding away in an orphanage. He was stubborn, argumentative….a total wise-guy, but he had a pure heart. Now, his identity established, Jaron will rule Carthya. He only needs to survive the attempts on his life and thwart the pirate invasion to do so.<br /><br />On the eve of his family’s funeral, Jaron learns that he has 10 days before the Avenian pirates, supported by King Vargan, wage war on Carthya. His army simply cannot prepare to defend his country in such a short time. His only choice is to stop the invasion. Thus begins a suspenseful adventure, packed with action and intrigue.<br /><br />While The Runaway King features thrilling sword fights, death-defying escape attempts and fool-hardy challenges, it also demonstrates strong-will, resolve and determination. All along his journey, Jaron is forced to evaluate the few people close to him. There are false loyalties, and they must be weeded out. Friendship needs to be re-established with Roden, the ferocious, vendetta-seeking enemy consumed by his desire to destroy Jaron. Above all, Jaron must protect those that have supported and assisted him along the way.<br /><br />To me, Jaron is the ultimate character for a Middle-Grade book. Outwardly, he appears flippant, arrogant and condescending. He may truly possess and exhibit those characteristics, but they are not the ones that define the person he is. Rather, the reader gets to know a determined young man that must pursue that which is right. With a heart so pure and true, Jaron is driven to protect those he cares about and the country that he loves. He is a fine example of a true hero. <br /><br />The Runaway King was just released in March, so I have no idea how long I will need to wait for the conclusion; but I am confident that, however, long; it will be worth the wait.<br /><br /> UPDATE: It WAS! It totally was worth the wait! The Shadow Throne could serve as a perfect example of what readers want, what we need from a conclusion. Review is coming soon!<br /><br /><br /> This review was written for Buried Under Books by jv poore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6542010742364997916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1547951106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547951106" />
    <a title="Masooma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma"><img alt="Masooma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455366226p2/26677122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547951106?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Masooma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Masooma" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma">Masooma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547951106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8197975057835209093">Right in front of you is a mouth-watering pudding which whispers promises of a guaranteed time in heaven with each bite but just as you've your first bite, you realize something is missing. You're sure tour taste buds made a mistake because looks can't be that deceiving, right? So you take another bite. This time toy realize something is definitely missing, maybe low sugar content. But you still eat because the same chef just yesterday made the best chocolate pie in the world and it's pudding af</span>
  <span id="freeText8197975057835209093" style="display:none">Right in front of you is a mouth-watering pudding which whispers promises of a guaranteed time in heaven with each bite but just as you've your first bite, you realize something is missing. You're sure tour taste buds made a mistake because looks can't be that deceiving, right? So you take another bite. This time toy realize something is definitely missing, maybe low sugar content. But you still eat because the same chef just yesterday made the best chocolate pie in the world and it's pudding after all, isn't it?<br /><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15703770.The_Runaway_King__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___2_" title="The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, #2) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Runaway King</a> was exactly this for me: a pudding without the right measurement of sugar or to be precise, a book without enough adrenaline.</b> And I read this just for my love for Sage just as I'd eat the pudding just for the sake of my love for desserts. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>So what happens:</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>The pirates wanted my life, Vargan wanted my country, and my reagents wanted to paint rainbows over reality and claim all was well.</i><br /><br />Bitter with the burden of a kingdom on his shoulders, the free-spirited boy-king Jaron finds himself in a tangled mess with lack of internal support, external threats and an unfavorable public pinion. In order to save the kingdom, Jaron decides to go from reckless to responsible by going to the lair of devils and in the least, reduce the threat of war from one side- the Pirates. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>So what went wrong:</i>
</b><br /><br />For one thing, when I heard of the pirates I went bananas with excitement. I knew some real awesome-ness was coming my way and given Sage's personality, it would be awesomeness with a layer of marvelous toppings.<br />But like they say: Never built castles in the air!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Why, I hear you say?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Because the pirates weren't as barbaric or dangerous or bonkers as you'd expect.</b> Rather they were an organized lot with a code of conduct and laws governing their world. And the pirate king was the most tolerant, patient and inexperienced villain I've ever met! <br /><br />Initially there was an expression of 'Nobody comes back from the pirates'. Now as a well-read reader, you know by experience that Jaron will come back but you'd expect it with the aid of a cunning-as-a-fox mind and the tricks of a devil.<br /><br />Rather everything happened with a stroke of luck, a bunch of coincidences and teddy-bear opponents. And frankly, a bit of nonsense <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[such as Imogen having easily penetrated the God-damn-dangerously-awful-pirates even before Jaron and tricking the sea monsters by knives all with zilch suspicious <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>There was nothing freaky or scary, no heart-hammering action, not a pinch of adrenaline and an unhealthy balance of descriptions and emotions in the writing.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Sage, you ask? What happened to my love for Sage?</i>
</b><br /><br />Well, I was head over heels when Jaron slipped back to Sage but Sages wits weren't cunning this time around. Although is big mouth is still as much fun but his brain failed to be impressive!<br /><br /><b>Other characters were okay-ish, just the usual type. Villains were easy-peasy as if simple fried eggs instead of an elaborate lasagna.</b> I liked Fink though, a boisterous, talkative character with a distinct style. Imogen and Amarinda stuck to their oath of being dry as bones characters.<br /><br />Finally <b>the romance. Although love with a base of friendship is the best treat a reader gets but in this case, there was no electricity zipping around.</b> So it's painful to admit but it was disappointing. In fact, I've grown to understand that Imogen's role is just as a pawn to get to Jaron. <br /><br /><b>Overall, an average read with a few injured expectations.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8197975057835209093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Experiment BL626" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626"><img alt="Experiment BL626" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335917426p2/4582872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441603183?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Experiment BL626" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Experiment BL626" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626">Experiment BL626</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441603183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16019929210093454475">After the awesomeness that was book 1 — read my review for book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223434721' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>, I held high expectation for book 2. Woah did I regret doing that. Book 2 exercised my suspension of disbelief hard. Immediately, there were signs portending disappointment. Towards the ending, they bloomed like prickly weeds, and I was left with a rather bitter taste as if I literally ate a weed.<br/><br/><b>+ the protagonist</b><br/>Jaron bugged me. He was rude to the people who didn’t deserve it. No, I did not care it was intended to distance and</span>
  <span id="freeText16019929210093454475" style="display:none">After the awesomeness that was book 1 — read my review for book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223434721" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>, I held high expectation for book 2. Woah did I regret doing that. Book 2 exercised my suspension of disbelief hard. Immediately, there were signs portending disappointment. Towards the ending, they bloomed like prickly weeds, and I was left with a rather bitter taste as if I literally ate a weed.<br /><br /><b>+ the protagonist</b><br />Jaron bugged me. He was rude to the people who didn’t deserve it. No, I did not care it was intended to distance and shield them from the danger of being around him. It was juvenile and short-sighted. The times when Jaron was kind, he was kind mostly to the people who didn’t deserve it. They should have been killed for the sake of his life <i>and</i> the relief of my great annoyance. Goodness was I annoyed! How many times does someone have to try to kill you before you accept the fact that they don’t just like you? Honestly.<br /><br />I stopped thinking Jaron was clever and started seeing him in full display as a Gary Stu. The plot forced itself to portray him as clever when in reality nothing he did was actually clever but instead was reckless. He succeeded only by an incredible amount of luck. So much luck that I swear I could hear the story’s internal logic cracking like an elephant on thin ice. How Jaron overcame obstacle after obstacle, each more seemingly insurmountable than the previous, was difficult to digest.<br /><br /><b>+ Roden</b><br />For 99% of the book, I could not understand for the life of me why Jaron insisted on obtaining Roden’s loyalty when Roden did nothing to earn it. Nothing at all. Roden was homicidal towards Jaron and not to mention useless. I was waiting for Roden to die like the expendable villain that he was. What happened to Jaron and Roden towards the end left me flabbergasted and steamed. When Jaron revealed his reasons for why he wanted Roden at the end, I immediately called bullshit. Utter, utter bullshit. I seriously questioned Jaron’s competence to rule as king. Hell, I questioned his intelligence; I think all that fighting and blood loss Jaron went through obliterated some brain cells.<br /><br /><b>+ the pirates</b><br />The book spent an inordinate amount of the plot developing the bad dudes’ fearsome reputation. When the reader, via Jaron, finally met them, they turned out to be less fearsome than the countryside robbers Jaron encountered in the middle of the book. These pirates respected and protected their female servants. They adhered to a pirate’s code and kept their promises like honorable knights. They weren’t greedy as they were said to be, because if they were they would have tortured Jason until he confessed the location of the kingdom’s treasury. They were basically good guys in bad guys’ clothes who were no more bloodthirsty than the average soldier. <br /><br />The only actual bad guy in the bunch was the leader of the pirates, and how things ended with him, so ridiculously contrived, made me want to slap somebody. It seriously discredited the leader as a swordmaster and cracked the plot’s internal logic some more. <br /><br /><b>+ the love triangle</b><br />I didn’t really believe there was a love triangle in book 1, but to my disgust book 2 proved me wrong. Imogen and Jaron like each other but can’t be together, because Jaron is a king and Amarinda is promised to be the king’s wife. The romance between Imogen and Jaron was about as convincing and real as a flying pig, and as terrible to read as if that flying pig shit on my head. I felt I got shit on some more when I read how the issue resolved itself. <br /><br />Isn’t this book supposed to be a Middle Grade? I know I tagged it Young Adult, but the publisher list the book as Middle Grade. Love triangle in a Middle Grade? Has Young Adult been infested by a nearby genre with its laziness?<br /><br /><b>+ Amarinda</b><br />I felt really bad for Amarinda. No one wanted her. Hell, it seemed like even the series doesn’t want her. She still played an important role in book 2, but barely. As the story progressed, it was getting to look like the character was introduced in the series as an afterthought. <br /><br />Book 2 never developed her beyond the tragic princess from some far away, forgettable kingdom book 1 established her to be. For all the talks about how Jaron’s kingdom was in danger and they have no allies, why did no one ever ask Amarinda’s kingdom for help? Why couldn’t Amarinda or Jaron break off the engagement? “Because the story said so” is not an answer, but that was what essentially was given. Did anyone ever bother to tell Amarinda’s kingdom that the dude she was supposed to marry, Jaron’s big brother, is dead, and Jaron is now her new fiance? If so, what did they think? Where were the political ramifications? Too many questions, and none of them answered. <br /><br />Once I started examining Amarinda’s backstory, I saw how poorly it was developed. I saw the lack of a strong reason for her character. I started cynically thinking the only reason she was in the series to make for a ridiculous, shitty love triangle. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion</b><br /><br />I rate <i>The Runaway King</i> 3 stars for I liked it. Surprised? Me too. In spite of all the issues, I managed to enjoy the story...somewhat. The pacing was fast so I never had a long moment to dwell on the issues as they popped up. There was a good twist, some wrapping up of loose ends, and great progress made in the series overall. I didn’t even mind the cliffhanger ending, though half of that was due to the lowering of expectation and subsequent loss of anticipation for the next book. One thing was for sure, I wasn’t bored at least.<br /><br />Fair warning. That 3 stars is provisional. I will downrate if book 3 sucks ass because how the series is overall affects my very subjective ratings. Hell, even book 1’s 5 stars rating is provisional. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16019929210093454475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

This series changed everything I've dreaded when reading a 2nd book because it is often times the downer,do you agree?<br/><br/>And now,I am telling you that this is the perfect sequel to the first book,that I found myself instantly drawn into the story as it picks up where the first one ended.   <span id="freeText13939198142576821230" style="display:none">I've never been so happy after reading a second book in a trilogy! This series changed everything I've dreaded when reading a 2nd book because it is often times the downer,do you agree?<br /><br />And now,I am telling you that this is the perfect sequel to the first book,that I found myself instantly drawn into the story as it picks up where the first one ended. And again,I loved everything in this book as the story and the adventures of the MC resumed to amaze me. If you loved SAGE in The False Prince,you'll surely love him even more here because of his braveness,strength,talent,and his cunningness or his strategic mind.<br /><br />In here,new characters were introduced including the pirates and the thieves who contributed a lot in the excitement and supense of the plot.But then,the supporting characters were always the ones who bring so much in the story,particulary my favorites:Mott,Imogen,Tobias,Amarinda,<br />plus Fink and Harlowe.<br /><br />There were heart pounding moments in this book where you would feel the panic,worry and fear for the MC,as he struggle to save his friends,his people and his country. There were times that I laughed out loud to some of Sage's amazing dialogues.And there were moments that I really cried because the author incredibly created a wonderful friendship in this sequel. <br />So yes! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3267859.Jennifer_A__Nielsen" title="Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer A. Nielsen</a> has done it again! You got to start reading this series now!^^<br /><br />To my friends who recommended this series to me,I'll be forever thankful to you <b>PANG,MUSE-IC,MASOOMA,and ALAFIYA</b> .You may also check their awesome reviews!^^</span>

<div id="review_557723426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/557723426" />
    <a title="Madison ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11828179-madison"><img alt="Madison ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362848574p2/11828179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/557723426?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madison ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madison ♡" href="/user/show/11828179-madison">Madison ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828179-madison?shelf=proreview">proreview</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer557723426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14399803844766352850">Curse you Jennifer A. Nielsen. Curse you for ripping out my heart and stepping on it and making me die a sad, bookless death. Ugh. <br/>Anyyyway, OH MY GOSH THIS BOOK WAS PERFECTION. <br/>Like, seriously. <br/>Okay, let's start with characters. Roden actually showed dimension! We didn't see much of Tobias, but I liked him when I read about him. Let's just say this: WHY DO ALL MY FAVORITE CHARACTERS BECOME EVIL OR DIE? Good thing my favorite character decided to be awesome in the end. <br/>Now, in my review for The </span>
  <span id="freeText14399803844766352850" style="display:none">Curse you Jennifer A. Nielsen. Curse you for ripping out my heart and stepping on it and making me die a sad, bookless death. Ugh. <br />Anyyyway, OH MY GOSH THIS BOOK WAS PERFECTION. <br />Like, seriously. <br />Okay, let's start with characters. Roden actually showed dimension! We didn't see much of Tobias, but I liked him when I read about him. Let's just say this: WHY DO ALL MY FAVORITE CHARACTERS BECOME EVIL OR DIE? Good thing my favorite character decided to be awesome in the end. <br />Now, in my review for The False Prince, I said I was nervous about the love triangle thing that would happen in this book. I am so glad to say that I had nothing to worry about. The romance was minimal. Small spoiler, though it is sort of obvious... [spoilers removed]. <br />Anyway, not much romance. Mostly just action and awesome and sweet glory. We don't see much of Amarinda, but I love reading it when she's in there. The nice friendship between Jaron and Amarinda is amazing, especially since they are meant to be married to each other. They both have small reasons to not love each other, but come to a mutual agreement, and I LOVE THEM. <br />But seriously, this book isn't about who should end up with who. <br />I actually liked this book more than The False Prince, which is saying something. Most of the time, second books aren't better than first. In my opinion, this was. Because there were [spoilers removed].<br />Okay, so, I probably shouldn't say this, but I feel like a love triangle will actually be prominent in the third book, just because the ending hints at it a lot. <br />I really like Amarinda and Imogen. Two of the most amazing female characters ever. Imogen does do what most typical YA female characters do (which is do the opposite of what they're told to do), but she actually apologizes for her mistakes. AND she actually had a reason to go against Jaron's orders. Sigh. Imogen and Amarinda are so perfect.<br />Roden was awesome. I was surprised at how much he changed from the first book. Luckily common sense stole him. Good, because he's awesome. <br />Jaron is amazing, as always. I love--LOVE--his sarcastic tone. He goes through a LOT in this book, but he always keeps that sarcasm. He thinks things through, but doesn't hint at thinking them through, if that makes sense. <br />So yeah. This book, The Runaway King, is amazing and flawless. Not much trouble with pacing at all. Seriously, this series stole my soul. I have to wait over a year to get the third book and this book left off with such an awful cliffhanger! I was scared to finish the book because I knew a cliffhanger would happen and it did.<br />So curse you Jennifer A. Nielsen. Curse you for writing such an amazing book. And curse you for making me wait to read the next installment. Curse you for making me read this book instead of doing homework. And lastly, curse you for making me fall in love with yet another fictional character. <br />Thanks for writing an awesome book. Can't wait for the next one. <br />Now it's time to hibernate until the next book comes out.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1541721946" />
    <a title="Alafiya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44560617-alafiya"><img alt="Alafiya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460842696p2/44560617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1541721946?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alafiya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alafiya" href="/user/show/44560617-alafiya">Alafiya</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541721946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9715832747206428601">P a t h e t i c.<br/><br/>Guys, I have a white flying unicorn. A flying unicorn that vomits ice-cream and is glittery. When it farts a genie appears that grants wishes. <br/>Do you believe me? Prolly not. I don't believe me either. But nice thought, eh? Exactly like this book. All sorts of unrealistic things happened in this book but somehow I liked it enough to give it three stars. <br/><br/>In this second instalment King Jaron is attacked. Not with affectionate hugs or something like that (pun intended) but an attempt</span>
  <span id="freeText9715832747206428601" style="display:none">P a t h e t i c.<br /><br />Guys, I have a white flying unicorn. A flying unicorn that vomits ice-cream and is glittery. When it farts a genie appears that grants wishes. <br />Do you believe me? Prolly not. I don't believe me either. But nice thought, eh? Exactly like this book. All sorts of unrealistic things happened in this book but somehow I liked it enough to give it three stars. <br /><br />In this second instalment King Jaron is attacked. Not with affectionate hugs or something like that (pun intended) but an attempt at assassinating him is made which forces him to desert his kingdom in order to save it. Also war is coming. How will Jaron outwit the devils with that little brain and large mouth of his? Or will he die trying to use his brain? Will he return to his kingdom? The synopsis makes this book sound too awesome. But compared to The False Prince this book is... *sighs* <i>uncool</i>. <br /><br />The plot was a mess. Like the author didn't know what to do next and everything that happened in favour of Jaron was pure glittery unicorn-y luck. Seriously, no logic at all. Jaron was adamant in proving what a schmuck he was. Everything was <i>too</i> convenient. The villain was like cotton candy. <i>All of the villains were like cotton candy.</i> There was <i>flat</i> romance. I'd rather have none than flat romance. Jaron acted like a fool. Everyone did. Made me come to this conclusion: <b>
  <i> It's not that Jaron is impressive, it's that every other character in this book is too unimpressive. </i>
</b> There were too many eye-roll moments (you can find them in the spoiler) Rest, the writing was beautiful and the dialogues were as awesome as they were in book 1. Somehow I enjoyed it a bit though nothing made any sense and man, I am so disappointed. <br /><br /> Now welcome to the spoiler-y part, here you'll find few of the things that had me rolling my eyes. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Let's start with Jaron and his absurdity. And no, I'm not going to smile, shake my head and defend his actions as those of a brave witty hero. Jaron wanted to kill all the pirates without a proper plan. Like what? Too much hollywood bollywood shiz. Jaron walked into lethal danger every time and came out alive. Then there was Amarinda, coward Amarinda, who sent Imogen to the pirates and said that Imogen volunteered while Imogen said that Amarinda sent her. What? Then there were thieves who basically didn't commit murder (because everything is so damn convenient) and pirates who didn't tease women instead protected their honour (because everything is so damn freaking convenient) the pirates who were another handful of candies. Oh boy! There was also this very cute bush that helped in numbing pain and was there at the right time and place. (because everything is so damn freaking flipping convenient) Everything just worked out. Don't even get me started on how dumb Jaron acted and how annoying all the female characters were including Nila. The pirate king was soo sweet he accepted Jaron despite how full of humility he was. Cute. &lt;3 Then Jaron won back Rodent, I mean Roden, and all went well. La la la. I have more ranting to do but I think this para is rather long so I'll just swallow it. Feel free to discuss. No wait I have to say this; I don't think that either the pirates or the rodent had a good enough reason to want to kill Jaron. Paper plot I tell ya. <i>sigh</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*clenches her jaw and walks out*<br /> </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle">beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369919806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6333245542408141784">The False prince was a fast and fun tale that had a nice twist at the end that made the book all the more enjoyable. While I liked the Runaway King it didn’t quite capture the same feel as the first book. Sage now Jaron is King of a land on the brink of war. But he isn’t quite the same boy, he is a little bit snarky with everyone around him to the point that it is almost annoying and slightly whiney. But I guess I might be a little hostile is someone tried to assassinate me in the very first cha</span>
  <span id="freeText6333245542408141784" style="display:none">The False prince was a fast and fun tale that had a nice twist at the end that made the book all the more enjoyable. While I liked the Runaway King it didn’t quite capture the same feel as the first book. Sage now Jaron is King of a land on the brink of war. But he isn’t quite the same boy, he is a little bit snarky with everyone around him to the point that it is almost annoying and slightly whiney. But I guess I might be a little hostile is someone tried to assassinate me in the very first chapter.<br /><br />Jaron isn’t sure who is really on his side and who is plotting against him. He seems to be getting mixed signals from everyone at this point. The only thing he seems to know for sure is that someone wants him dead. Jaron made some classic MG moves and not much of the story seemed to be surprising. I am an adult though so I think I caught a lot of the hints early on.<br /><br />I had more fun with the story once Jaron went back to being Sage and ran away to try and figure out how to stall the war. He was back to his mischievous self and causing trouble for everyone he met. There are a few new characters Fink being the most fun and possibly a younger version of our Sage in some ways. Street rat to the max he has a tender heart and just wants to find his place in the world too. While they have a rough start I like how Sage feels almost responsible for him later, almost like a big brother.<br /><br />Imogen is still one of my favorite characters in the series as she is so loyal and always there to help Sage get out of the terrible trouble he gets himself into. But the ending leaves it very up in the air as to how her story arc will ultimately play out. <br /><br />I’d like to get a chance to actually see Jaron as King and how he deals with pulling his country together for a war. I’m also very interested in the dynamic between Imogen Jaron and Amaranth and how the relationship aspect of the story will all work out.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8159283581875582438"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Everyone gets scared at times. It's only the fools who won't admit it.” </i> </b><br/><br/><b> SPOILERS IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THE FIRST BOOK! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!!! </b><br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/>The Runaway King picks up quickly where The False Prince left off. Sage revealed himself to be Prince Jaron in hiding all along and he is crowned king. When threats from other countries become a fast issue, Jaron must risk everything to save this country and his people. And that’s all I will say from here…<br/><br/><b> <i> “Above all else, I think th</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText8159283581875582438" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “Everyone gets scared at times. It's only the fools who won't admit it.” </i> </b><br><br><b> SPOILERS IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THE FIRST BOOK! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!!! </b><br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>The Runaway King picks up quickly where The False Prince left off. Sage revealed himself to be Prince Jaron in hiding all along and he is crowned king. When threats from other countries become a fast issue, Jaron must risk everything to save this country and his people. And that’s all I will say from here…<br><br><b> <i> “Above all else, I think that you are a compulsive liar."<br>My laughter was tense, but sincere. “Hardly. In fact, I consider myself a compulsive truth teller. It's only that everyone else seems compelled to misunderstand me.” </i> </b><br><br>I didn’t like this book as much as the first book, I actually found myself putting it down and choosing to do other things instead. It definitely picked back up in the second half and that’s what saved the book for me. I like Jaron so much as a narrator and a protagonist, he has this wonderful, wry sense of humor. I like that despite being a troublemaker he wants the best for his country and his people and is willing to put everything on the line for him.<br><br>Definitely going to read the last book.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355607544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17327478733244890518">Flashback to 2012: <em>
  <a href='http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2012/04/false-prince-ascendance-trilogy-1-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The False Prince</a>
</em> was coming out, and I really, really wanted to read it.  It had been a long time since I'd been so excited for the release of a non-sequel book.  And when I finally read it, it was awesome.  Not five-stars awesome, but pretty close.  <br/><br/>And then this book happened.  It's rare for a sequel to improve on its predecessor, but Jennifer Nielson pulled it off.  I applaud her for that.  At this rate, the finale of this series will be utterly fabulous.<br/><br/>This book is ju</span>
  <span id="freeText17327478733244890518" style="display:none">Flashback to 2012: <em>
  <a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2012/04/false-prince-ascendance-trilogy-1-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The False Prince</a>
</em> was coming out, and I really, really wanted to read it.  It had been a long time since I'd been so excited for the release of a non-sequel book.  And when I finally read it, it was awesome.  Not five-stars awesome, but pretty close.  <br><br>And then this book happened.  It's rare for a sequel to improve on its predecessor, but Jennifer Nielson pulled it off.  I applaud her for that.  At this rate, the finale of this series will be utterly fabulous.<br><br>This book is just so much <em>fun</em>.  It's just a sheer pleasure to read.  I'm not entirely sure what designates a book as "fun"--a good book is not necessarily fun, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/3984780?shelf=so-much-fun" rel="nofollow noopener">a fun book is always good</a>.  <em>The Marbury Lens</em> or <em>The Giver</em>, for example, are excellent books, but they don't have this element of fun to them.  Part of the appeal, I think, is that no matter how intense this book gets, it never forgets to lighten up every so often.  It can make you smile.  It's a swashbuckling (and yes, there are pirates, so I am absolutely allowed to call it "swashbuckling") adventure with plenty of witty dialogue.<br><br>All of this would have easily earned this book four stars.  And yet, I'm giving it five.  Here's why, in one word:<br><br>JARON.<br><br>It's been a long time since I loved a main character this much.  Part of it, I think, is the fact that he reminds me of my own main character, more so than any other character I've read about before.  He has a very similar situation in life to my MC, so that makes him easy for me to like.  <br><br>Also, he can be hilarious when he gets going.  <br>Jaron: "I want the [sword] I came here with."<br>Pirate: "Why that one?"<br>Jaron: "The stones in the handle match my eyes."<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://media.tumblr.com/tumblr_m5kp54L2BC1rpzld6.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="150" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381930ra/739393.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>Oh, Jaron.  So quirky, and yet...there is some awesome depth to him.  The author did not skimp on her character development, that's for sure.  Another part of the reason why I love him so much is that he spouts all these one-liners because a) it's just who he is and b) I think he wants to cover something up.  He's had to go through some tough things, and these experiences take their toll.  Smart-aleck is his coping method.  Jennifer Nielson does a wonderful job ensuring that all of these emotions get through to the reader.  <br><br>And, as always, there's an element of "I just like this character because <em>reasons</em>."  You can't pinpoint exactly why you like them, or what you like about them, but you love them all the same.  And Jaron is totally the kind of character where I would like to pull him out of his book and hang out with him, because he's just awesome.<br><strong></strong><br><strong> <div>
<br><a href="http://applejack.ponychan.net/chan/files/src/136148598497.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381930ra/739394.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div>
<br></strong><br><br>I loved this book.  It sits in that no-man's land between middle grade and young adult.  Well, I shouldn't call it a no-man's land, because I'm rather fond of it.  Anyway, though, it fits into that, er, spot, but it would definitely appeal to older YA readers.  You're never too old for some MG, or this fabulous book.  <br><br>Five stars because Jaron.  And the rest of it, too.<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-QaQ-r5WfZ64/TieNAXcI9fI/AAAAAAAAAHI/9BNrIBFVh18/s1600/five+stars.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="98" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347960i/702295.png" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br><strong>Similar Books: </strong>It has a very similar premise to <em><a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2013/01/falling-kingdoms-falling-kingdoms-1-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a></em>, has a plucky young teenage boy hero like the <a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2012/05/hold-me-closer-necromancer-fear-and.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ranger's Apprentice books</a><em>, </em>and feels similar to <em><a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2012/03/girl-of-fire-and-thorns-fire-and-thorns.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a>.  </em>It would be a fabulous read for someone who likes high fantasy of this sort but is too young for (or who just wants something tamer than) <em><a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com/2012/10/a-game-of-thrones-song-of-ice-and-fire.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>.</em>
</div><br><br>Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://anniesepicblog.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Epic, the Awesome, and the Random</a>.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17327478733244890518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9701000983350494726" style="display:none">This was of a similar quality to the first book in the series. It was a fast paced and fun read even if it does not have the most complex of plots. This is a book aimed at younger readers so the heroes a heroes and the villains are villains! Despite that the characters are a likeable and interesting bunch and the plot held my attention. <br /><br />The story picks up where things ended in The False Prince with Jaron now being crowned King. Unfortunately for Jaron this is just the start of his problems as neighbouring countries sense a weakness, the pirates that tried to assassinate him as a child resurface and are determine to finish the job, and Jaron's own regents are trying to usurp his leadership. Luckily for Jaron he has a few old friends like Mott, Imogen and Tobias to help him deal with his growing list of problems!<br /><br />This was an enjoyable read and the story ended on a bit of a cliffhanger so the third book should be exciting.<br /><br />Rating : 3.5 stars<br /><br />Audio Note: This was narrated well by Charlie McWade. He is a good fit for Jaron and seems to get the tone of the story. </span>

  <span id="freeText10059124588631493846" style="display:none">To be honest, I didn’t like this one as much as the first. Don’t get me wrong, it was really good, I just didn’t like it as much. Like? Okay? Why tho? Ironically Roden was one of my favorite characters, but it still didn’t quite feel right... just me? Yeahhhh probably 😂<br />(END SPOILER)<br /><br />But yeah! That’s basically it! There is mild violence btw<br /><br />Happy reading guys!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15020970916753164013">3.5-4 stars. It was a slow read for awhile, the first half of the book seemed to drag on a bit. However it's a quick read and the last 100 pages or so definitely make up for the previous 200. I really think this is another example of second book syndrome, it just didn't come close to being as good as the false prince, and kind of left me feeling like I wanted more. (which is a good thing in a trilogy I guess?) I mean it's still a really good book and I'm super excited for the third, so it succee</span>
  <span id="freeText15020970916753164013" style="display:none">3.5-4 stars. It was a slow read for awhile, the first half of the book seemed to drag on a bit. However it's a quick read and the last 100 pages or so definitely make up for the previous 200. I really think this is another example of second book syndrome, it just didn't come close to being as good as the false prince, and kind of left me feeling like I wanted more. (which is a good thing in a trilogy I guess?) I mean it's still a really good book and I'm super excited for the third, so it succeeded in that aspect but I just could have gone for some more substance. I feel like the plot line in this one just kind of came about too easily. Anyway definitely recommend it as the story overall between the two novels is fantastic, and I love the characters! Looking forward to the next! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_921782964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/921782964" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/921782964?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=bad-book-makes-me-feel-bad">bad-book-makes-me-feel-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer921782964&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer921782964" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18254298860173113284">So I read the first two-thirds of this book in a few days, it then took me another 2-3 weeks to manage to finish it. Having read the first book and considered it a good, if somewhat flawed, young adult book I was really disappointed in reading this one. If I hadn't read the first book and thought it was pretty good I probably wouldn't have persevered with this one.<br/><br/>The awkward pacing of the first book returned in this one. The author again imposed a short timetable on events and seemed to struggl</span>
  <span id="freeText18254298860173113284" style="display:none">So I read the first two-thirds of this book in a few days, it then took me another 2-3 weeks to manage to finish it. Having read the first book and considered it a good, if somewhat flawed, young adult book I was really disappointed in reading this one. If I hadn't read the first book and thought it was pretty good I probably wouldn't have persevered with this one.<br /><br />The awkward pacing of the first book returned in this one. The author again imposed a short timetable on events and seemed to struggle to fit the plot into it. The unreliable narrator technique that was used in the first book was toned down unfortunately the intelligent characterisation and solid plot of the first book also doesn't reappear. <br /><br />(Be advised the rest of this review is mostly a rant about the stupid character decisions/ plot devices in this book. Also Spoilers) The book starts as injustice strikes the peaceful nation of Carthya. The wise king Jaron, a 15 year old boy who was sent to boarding school in a faraway land when he was 10 for being really annoying and has spent the last 5 years living as a street urchin, is forced from his throne by evil nobles who think that he is unfit to rule and that a more experienced, mature steward should rule as regent until he comes of age. I know what you're thinking: that's completely ridonc. Jaron is really good at climbing stuff, of course he should have absolute control over the running of an entire country. But Jaron refuses to have his power taken from him. Instead of doing something stupid like using his wealth and power as the sole remaining scion of the royal family to begin a campaign of bribery, blackmail, manipulation and intimidation on the 20 nobles who's votes he needs to secure his position he does something way more befitting a king. He goes on an adventure! With Pirates!<br /><br />So Jaron goes to see the pirates who fortunately turn out to be pretty much Disney characters. They skip singing a jaunty tune and get straight to explaining the 'pirate code'. Essentially while they're allowed to steal and murder (they are the villains) they aren't allowed to harm women or children. Also despite their base being filled with testosterone-fuelled raiders with no other women in sight for miles the young, pretty serving girls are completely safe from harm. I appreciate this is YA but it kinda undermines your 'lair of evil villains' credibility when they're nicer than your average group of fighters throughout history. <br /><br />Another star turn comes from Gregor, the ruthless political mastermind who outwitted Jaron in forcing him off his throne. Unfortunately Gregor is cunningly outmaneuvered in turn when he leaves his country, in the middle of the 10 days of voting that will decide if he realizes his ambitions of becoming regent, to travel to the base of the untrustworthy pirates he is conspiring with. Alone. Without any guards. At all. When he arrives, after giving a brief summary to everyone in earshot of his evil doings the pirate leader springs a bold, unexpected surprise by ordering the valuable, completely unguarded potential hostage/ dangerous loose end in the middle of their camp seized. Realizing the betrayal only too late Gregor reminds him of the sacred pact they made: 'but we pinky swore!'. The evil pirate then revealed the true depths of his treachery... he had his fingers crossed the whole time!!! <br /><br />The pirate king also gets a special shoutout as a magnet of stupidity. First Jaron decides not to kill him because he's too much of a good guy even though allowing him to live will mean that he brings death and destruction to Jaron's subjects and the pirate himself is a complete scumbag. Then when he realizes Jaron's deception and is about to have him executed he instead agrees to duel Jaron. The pirate king had nothing to gain fighting a guy already his captive and everything to lose, however when Jaron reminds him about 'pirate code' the king, fearing pirate litigation in pirate court and possibly even being sent to pirate jail agrees to fight him. And promptly gets beaten by a 15 year old. Natch. <br /><br />On the brightside I really liked Imogen as a character. She was smart, brave and seemed to genuinely care about Jaron and tried to deter him from his dumbass plans. My favourite character was Roden. After his(really stupid) defeat last time he spent much of the book as a villain. Our knowledge of his difficult background and his basic decency made him a somewhat sympathetic villain and he served up the 2 most badass moments in the book. First when he cut his way through a score of pirates to slay the pirate king with almost contemptuous ease. The second was the precautionary measure he took to keep Jaron from escaping. In a subversion of the bond-villainesque approach taken by most people in this series Roden just breaks Jaron's leg. Simple, brutal and effective. Or at least it would be effective if it hadn't been done on Mary Sue Jaron. A 15 year old prince who can scale a sheer vertical cliff face with a broken leg before defeating the deadliest warrior among the pirates in single combat. Roden's ultimate heel-face turn was predictable but still disappointing. His turn to evil, which was borne out of his wounded pride at having been beaten by Jaron was reversed by being beaten by Jaron again, this time with a broken leg. <br /><br />I know that this is a YA book and that even in regular fantasy, plot-twists are often contrived but I still found way too many disappointing flaws in both characterisation and plot in this book to enjoy it. 1000 characters of mocking and poking holes in a book written for younger readers was pretty tiring. I think I'm gonna go outside for a bit, play soccer or something, get some fresh air.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18254298860173113284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_470168877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/470168877" />
    <a title="Daphne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9006331-daphne"><img alt="Daphne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358661703p2/9006331.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/470168877?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daphne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daphne" href="/user/show/9006331-daphne">Daphne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9006331-daphne?shelf=must-reads">must-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9006331-daphne?shelf=kickass-protags">kickass-protags</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9006331-daphne?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer470168877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10972852737462879353">My reaction when I was accepted by Netgalley:<br/><br/><a href='http://s806.beta.photobucket.com/user/lilypad12345678901/media/tumblr_mh3m8c7JlD1rn7wkmo1_400_zpsc9a57973.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399760ra/773944.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mh3m8c7JlD1rn7wkmo1_400_zpsc9a57973.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/> <br/>The first novel in the Ascendance Trilogy, The False Prince, literally changed my life forever. Every time I was caught in a sticky situation, I immediately asked myself, "What would Sage do?" In fact, I was surprised that I even had the ability to talk coherently or function like a normal human being after I finished it. Jennifer Nielsen is that good! So when I saw that the sequel already had a epic name and donned a simple yet intriguing cover,</span>
  <span id="freeText10972852737462879353" style="display:none">My reaction when I was accepted by Netgalley:<br><br><a href="http://s806.beta.photobucket.com/user/lilypad12345678901/media/tumblr_mh3m8c7JlD1rn7wkmo1_400_zpsc9a57973.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399760ra/773944.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mh3m8c7JlD1rn7wkmo1_400_zpsc9a57973.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>The first novel in the Ascendance Trilogy, The False Prince, literally changed my life forever. Every time I was caught in a sticky situation, I immediately asked myself, "What would Sage do?" In fact, I was surprised that I even had the ability to talk coherently or function like a normal human being after I finished it. Jennifer Nielsen is that good! So when I saw that the sequel already had a epic name and donned a simple yet intriguing cover, I was absolutely ecstatic! If I had to wait another whole year just in order to get my hands onto The Runaway King, I would've probably broke down sobbing uncontrollably. Still, three to four months is a hell of a long time to wait when your this excited about something. I'm sure my fellow bookworms here would know what I'm talking about. ;) And I'm so relieved that Jennifer decided not to end The False Prince on one of those jaw dropping cliffhangers. If she had, I would've spent a long time staring despondently at a wall with thoughts running rampant, trying to figure out where the story would go next.<br> <br>Now if you've read The False Prince, I have no doubts in my mind that you have already fallen in love with Sage, our protagonist and the heir to the throne of Carthya. And if your a guy? Well, I have no idea how a guy's mind works, but I'm guessing that you would love to have him as a best friend. I had such a hard time picturing Sage as a fifteen year old boy in The False Prince, because he talked and acted in a way that seemed beyond his years. Forced to grow up just to survive the horrendous world he lived in. But after getting to know him better in The Runaway King, his crazy antics and unrealistic goals helped me remember just how young he really is. <br> <br>Now don't get me wrong, he's still quick on his toes, compassionate to the less fortunate, and as smartass as he ever was. But, even though he can be wise when he wants to be, he also has a tendency to do impulsive and irrational things. To go through with plans even when he has no chance of winning.This flaw, amongst others, made me believe that he wasn't some perfect prodigy prince ready to take on the world. He's made mistakes, a lot of them I might add, but he makes them in his own unique way, and always has good intentions. He realizes that he's not invincible, that he can get hurt, that others can get hurt because of him, and finally admits to himself that he's not always right. He grows as a character throughout this novel, and I was super impressed by how it was all executed. <br> <br>The humor! Oh the humor! Sage is the type of person to crack jokes at the most inappropriate times! Almost everything he said had a sarcastic undertone and that had me laughing through a good chunk of the book! Although I did find the comedy in The False Prince to be a smidge better, The Runaway King was a worthy contender! <br> <br>The romance. While there was close to no romance at all in the first book, we see a deeper connection grow throughout The Runaway King. I don't think it's a spoiler to mention who the lucky girl is since it was pretty much implied in The False Prince, but if you don't know who she is, then spoilers up ahead! Imogen was not the damsel in distress. She was a strong, independent girl who wasn't afraid to tell Sage off, even if he was the King of all of Carthya. Some people might find that ostentatious title a little intimidating, but Imogen never hesitated when she had to knock a little bit of common sense into Sage's sometimes thick head. She was intelligent, a think things through type of gal who definitely is a perfect fit for Sage! <br> <br>However, even though there is a romance in this book, it's very subtle and makes sense. Not one of those wretched Insta-Love connections when two people are "destined to be with each other." I know a lot of guys are put off by the relationship stuff that seems to be present in every single YA novel, but this one wasn't like that at all! It was plot driven rather that love driven. If I had to compare the relationship between Sage and Imogen with characters from another book, it would have to be that of Percy and Annabeth in the prominent Percy Jackson series.<br> <br>The Runaway King dragged me in from the very first page! I had to curb the urge to sneak my Kindle into Trigonometry to read in front of my math book instead of learning quadratic equations. xD Although I did successfully stop myself from reading by repeating the mantra, "Don't turn on the Kindle. Don't turn on the Kindle." over and over again in my head, I finally lost the mental battle warring in my head during Spanish class in hopes of finding out what happened next. Sadly, I was so absorbed with the happenings that were occuring, that I failed to notice when the teacher called on me. Suffice to say, my Kindle got taken away. -_- Back to what I was saying, you can never get tired of the intriguing fantasy world that Jennifer created, filled to the brim with dark secrets, treacherous politics, assassination attempts, and heart pounding sword fights.<br> <br>Overall, although I didn't hyperventilate over The Runaway King as much as I did The False Prince, it was still a worthy action filled sequel that satisfied my almost unreasonable high expectations. This is one of those novels that I would recommend to anyone, including guys, and especially if your a fellow Percy Jackson fan like myself. This captivating series doesn't focus on the romance aspect, but instead spotlights the mind gripping action and high stake chases. A very refreshing read to those who are tired of the same old typical love driven YA novel!<br> <br>Favorite Quotes:<br> <br>"Everyone gets scared at times. It's only the fools who won't admit it."<br> -The Runaway King by Jennifer Nielsen<br> <br>"Wherever our lives lead us, one thing is certain. You and I will always be connected. You might be able to deny that, but I can't. Even I am not that good a liar." <br>-The Runaway King by Jennifer Nielsen<br> <br>Hero- 5/5<br>Romance- 5/5<br>Action- 5/5<br>Comedy- 4.5/5<br>Writing Style- 5/5<br>Overall- 5/5<br><br><br>*An ebook copy was provided by Netgalley<br>in exchange for a honest and thoughtful review.*<br><br>For more reviews, visit my website <a href="http://readinguntildawn.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading Until Dawn.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10972852737462879353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1540391906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540391906" />
    <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay"><img alt="Nicay (dearnicay)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602162853p2/36178759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540391906?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicay (dearnicay)" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay">Nicay (dearnicay)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17454892-the-runaway-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36178759-nicay-dearnicay?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540391906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14925646277798372989"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449654468i/17320822._SX540_.png' width='350' height='100' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>After Jaron, the new King took his throne in Carthya, it didn’t end well as I think. Everyone except the one he knows didn’t agree with his control over the country. Many of them gave their opinions that he was reckless in terms of decision making and he was too young to be a King. And the regents decided that he must replace by a steward or a representative in the throne until he is ready to take it. The regents especially the captain didn’t believe there would be an attack in Carthya by th</span>
  <span id="freeText14925646277798372989" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449654468i/17320822._SX540_.png" width="350" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>After Jaron, the new King took his throne in Carthya, it didn’t end well as I think. Everyone except the one he knows didn’t agree with his control over the country. Many of them gave their opinions that he was reckless in terms of decision making and he was too young to be a King. And the regents decided that he must replace by a steward or a representative in the throne until he is ready to take it. The regents especially the captain didn’t believe there would be an attack in Carthya by the Avenia and the pirates. Until all of sudden, he must do everything to prove them that they were wrong and he will do anything to save the country from falling.<br><br>As I continue to read the second book of the Ascendance trilogy, I saw the deeper side of Jaron and his new responsibilities as the new King of Carthya, but the Jaron I knew was still there - reckless, clever and strong in case of problems occur. <br><br>But honestly, the story took so long before the action came up and when it does, the excitement really fades away. I still love the conclusion of the book, but I just expected some more. The characters especially Jaron, as I said was still amusing as he did the last time, but as I realized there were times that his decisions were not as good as it seems. He’s reckless, but I understand it. I just wish he will be improving in the final book.<br><br>All in all, I still liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15703770.The_Runaway_King__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___2_" title="The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, #2) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Runaway King</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3267859.Jennifer_A__Nielsen" title="Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer A. Nielsen</a>. More intense scenes and the enemies really emerged in this story. And I’m so excited to know what will be the final conclusion of this fantasy.<br><br><blockquote>
<a href="http://queennicaybooks.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Wordpress</a>┃<a href="http://instagram.com/thenerdysideofaqueen" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ┃ <a href="http://twitter.com/queennicay" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ┃ <a href="http://queennicay.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14925646277798372989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_582583098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582583098" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2895577-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256984502p2/2895577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582583098?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/2895577-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582583098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10159621014329816703">It wasn't a good sign when I hit a scene a few pages into the book and actually put it down to sigh in disappointment. After really loving the False Prince, how could I be so disenchanted with the Runaway King?<br/><br/>In the first book, Sage is interesting because he has some sort of secret agenda that crops up in weird actions and inexplicable skill sets. It's great, and I was hooked. But here? Here he is just rude and stupid. He does dumb things supposedly with a master plan in mind, and I think it's </span>
  <span id="freeText10159621014329816703" style="display:none">It wasn't a good sign when I hit a scene a few pages into the book and actually put it down to sigh in disappointment. After really loving the False Prince, how could I be so disenchanted with the Runaway King?<br /><br />In the first book, Sage is interesting because he has some sort of secret agenda that crops up in weird actions and inexplicable skill sets. It's great, and I was hooked. But here? Here he is just rude and stupid. He does dumb things supposedly with a master plan in mind, and I think it's supposed to have the same secret-agenda flavor of the first book, but it doesn't gel here. Jaron is awful to his friends, never explains anything, is rash and impulsive and for a boy who was SO calculating and controlled in book 1, here he just looks like a fool. It doesn't help that it's perfectly obvious how the rest of the book is going to unfold at the 1/4 mark. And then there's a tacked-on cliffhanger, which by the way is ALSO stupid, as anyone in their right mind would have seen it coming a mile away. <br /><br />The first book felt like a YA novel that an adult could enjoy. This one plants itself firmly in early-teen territory and doesn't budge. I'm just really disappointed about this - I was thrilled to see it had been published and downloaded it ASAP, but now a third will be a library loan at best. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10159621014329816703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k1v7uJ8Hkq6u3cKtDevYaayRRBPrZ5tuJUe3UgpvSR/OqktAl/ve5dLVM2xLBxfRMJpB4GkXzpO1ES3G6VigBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('73lMu8IUZkbVI+ZXYqoVg/Kc84bcSWljEGhY2CFZn9CyiPxDyugqDakrF5YkRto7bpf2dV45PJ6APsJMwm52yg==')})
  }

Torn between loyalty to the princess and her new friends\' ideas, between an old love and a new crush, and between her small mountain home and the bustling city, Miri looks to find her own way in this new place. Picking up where Princess Academy left off, and celebrating the joys of friendship, romance and the fate of fairy tale kingdoms, this new book delivers the completely delightful new story that fans
